   <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Rediviva" title="Columbia Rediviva">\n           Columbia\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         (1773)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Status\n        </th>\n        <td>\n scope="row">\n         Distance travelled\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         201,497,772 km (125,204,911 miles)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Satellites deployed\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         8\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Vehicle_Designation" title="Orbiter Vehicle Designation">\n        Orbiter Vehicle Designation\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        OV-102\n       </b>\n       ) was the first space-rated\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_orbiter" title="Space Shuttle orbiter">\n        orbiter\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       fleet. It launched for the first time on mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       on April 12, 1981, the first flight of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       . Over 22 years of service it completed 27 missions before\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        disintegrating during re-entry\n       </a>\n       near the end of its 28th mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       on February 1, 2003, resulting in the deaths of all seven crew members.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Construction began on\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       in 1975 at\n       <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_International" title="Rockwell International">\n        Rockwell International\n       </a>\n       \'s (formerly\n       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aviation" title="North American Aviation">\n        North American Aviation\n       </a>\n       /North American Rockwell) principal assembly facility in\n       <a href="/wiki/Palmdale,_California" title="Palmdale, California">\n        Palmdale, California\n       </a>\n       , a suburb of Los Angeles.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was named after the American\n       <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">\n        sloop\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Rediviva" title="Columbia Rediviva">\n         Columbia Rediviva\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       which, from 1787 to 1793, under the command of\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gray_(sea_captain)" title="Robert Gray (sea captain)">\n        Captain Robert Gray\n       </a>\n       , explored the US Pacific Northwest and became the first American vessel to circumnavigate the globe. It is also named after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">\n        Command Module\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n        Apollo 11\n       </a>\n       , the first manned landing on another celestial body.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA.2C_2003_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA.2C_2003-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was also the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_(personification)" title="Columbia (personification)">\n        female symbol\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . After construction, the orbiter arrived at\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       on March 25, 1979, to prepare for its first launch.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was originally scheduled to lift off in late 1979, however the launch date was delayed by problems with both the SSME components, as well as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_protection_system" title="Thermal protection system">\n        thermal protection system\n       </a>\n       (TPS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTRS_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NTRS-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On March 19, 1981, during preparations for a ground test,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_accidents_and_incidents#Other_non-astronaut_fatalities" title="Space accidents and incidents">\n        workers were asphyxiated\n       </a>\n       while working in Columbia\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       -purged aft engine compartment, resulting in (variously reported) two or three fatalities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:566175main_columbia-opf.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2670" data-file-width="2136" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/566175main_columbia-opf.jpg/170px-566175main_columbia-opf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/566175main_columbia-opf.jpg/255px-566175main_columbia-opf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/566175main_columbia-opf.jpg/340px-566175main_columbia-opf.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:566175main_columbia-opf.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         in the Orbiter Processing Facility after delivery to Kennedy Space Center in 1979. About 8 thousand of 30,000 tiles still had to be installed.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gebhardt.2C_2011_7-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Gebhardt.2C_2011-7">\n           [7]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first flight of\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       ) was commanded by\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Young_(astronaut)" title="John Young (astronaut)">\n        John Young\n       </a>\n       , a veteran from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Gemini\n       </a>\n       and Apollo programs who was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">\n        ninth person to walk on the Moon\n       </a>\n       in 1972, and piloted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Crippen" title="Robert Crippen">\n        Robert Crippen\n       </a>\n       , a rookie astronaut originally selected to fly on the military\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_Orbital_Laboratory" title="Manned Orbital Laboratory">\n        Manned Orbital Laboratory\n       </a>\n       (MOL) spacecraft, but transferred to NASA after its cancellation, and served as a support crew member for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo\xe2\x80\x93Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo-Soyuz\n       </a>\n       missions.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       spent 610 days in the Orbiter Processing Facility (OPF), another 35 days in the Vehicle Assembly Building (VAB), and 105 days on Pad 39A before finally lifting off.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTRS_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NTRS-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was successfully launched on April 12, 1981, the 20th anniversary of the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        human spaceflight\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </a>\n       ), and returned on April 14, 1981, after orbiting the Earth 36 times, landing on the dry lakebed runway at\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n        Edwards Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       in California.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       then undertook three further research missions to test its technical characteristics and performance. Its first operational mission, with a four-man crew, was\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-5" title="STS-5">\n        STS-5\n       </a>\n       , which launched on November 11, 1982. At this point\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was joined by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n         Challenger\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which flew the next three shuttle missions, while\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       underwent modifications for the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">\n        Spacelab\n       </a>\n       mission.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2284" data-file-width="2920" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg/220px-NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg/330px-NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg/440px-NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_salutes_Reagans.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         astronauts\n         <a href="/wiki/Ken_Mattingly" title="Ken Mattingly">\n          Thomas K. Mattingly\n         </a>\n         and Pilot\n         <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hartsfield" title="Henry Hartsfield">\n          Henry Hartsfield\n         </a>\n         salute President\n         <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">\n          Ronald Reagan\n         </a>\n         , standing beside his wife,\n         <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Reagan" title="Nancy Reagan">\n          Nancy\n         </a>\n         , upon landing in 1982.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1983,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       , under the command of John Young on what was his sixth spaceflight, undertook its second operational mission (\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-9" title="STS-9">\n        STS-9\n       </a>\n       ), in which the Spacelab science laboratory and a six-person crew was carried, including the first non-American astronaut on a space shuttle,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ulf_Merbold" title="Ulf Merbold">\n        Ulf Merbold\n       </a>\n       . After the flight,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       spent 18 months at the Rockwell Palmdale facility beginning in January 1984, undergoing modifications that removed the Orbiter Flight Test hardware and bringing it up to similar specifications as those of its sister orbiters. At that time the shuttle fleet was expanded to include\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n         Discovery\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n         Atlantis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       returned to space on January 12, 1986, with the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-61-C" title="STS-61-C">\n        STS-61-C\n       </a>\n       . The mission\'s crew included Dr.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_Chang-Diaz" title="Franklin Chang-Diaz">\n        Franklin Chang-Diaz\n       </a>\n       , as well as the first sitting member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       to venture into space,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Nelson_(politician)" title="Bill Nelson (politician)">\n        Bill Nelson\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The next shuttle mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">\n        STS-51-L\n       </a>\n       , was undertaken by\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       . It was launched on January 28, 1986, ten days after STS-61-C had landed, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        ended in disaster\n       </a>\n       73 seconds after launch. In the aftermath NASA\'s shuttle timetable was disrupted, and\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was not flown again until 1989 (on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-28" title="STS-28">\n        STS-28\n       </a>\n       ), after which it resumed normal service as part of the shuttle fleet.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-93" title="STS-93">\n        STS-93\n       </a>\n       , launched on July 23, 1999, was the first U.S. space mission with a female commander, Lt. Col.\n       <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Collins" title="Eileen Collins">\n        Eileen Collins\n       </a>\n       . This mission deployed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chandra_X-ray_Observatory" title="Chandra X-ray Observatory">\n        Chandra X-ray Observatory\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'\n       </i>\n       s final successful mission was\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-109" title="STS-109">\n        STS-109\n       </a>\n       , the fourth servicing mission for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       . Its next mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       , culminated in the\n       <a href="#Final_mission_and_destruction">\n        orbiter\'s loss\n       </a>\n       when it disintegrated during reentry, killing all seven of its crew.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Consequently, President Bush decided to retire the Shuttle orbiter fleet by 2010 in favor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">\n        Constellation program\n       </a>\n       and its manned\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion spacecraft\n       </a>\n       . The Constellation program was later cancelled with the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Authorization_Act_of_2010" title="NASA Authorization Act of 2010">\n        NASA Authorization Act of 2010\n       </a>\n       signed by President Obama on October 11.\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:left;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_milestones">\n    </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prototype_orbiter">\n        Prototype orbiter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prototype orbiter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           needs additional citations for\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verification\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please help\n           <a Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (April 2012)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3000" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg/330px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg/440px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         launching during\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n          STS-1\n         </a>\n         . Its distinctive black chines and "USA" painted on the starboard wing are visible.\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         was the only orbiter launched with its\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n          external tank\n         </a>\n         painted white, which was later discontinued to save weight.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Weight">\n        Weight\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Weight">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As the second orbiter to be constructed, and the first able to fly into space,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was roughly 8,000\xc2\xa0lb (3,600\xc2\xa0kg) heavier than subsequent orbiters such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , which were of a slightly different design, and had benefited from advances in materials technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In part, this was due to heavier wing and fuselage spars, the weight of early test instrumentation that remained fitted to the avionics suite, and an internal airlock that, originally fitted into the other orbiters, was later removed in favor of an external airlock to facilitate Shuttle/\n       <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n        Mir\n       </a>\n       and Shuttle/\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       dockings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to its weight,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       could not have used the planned\n       <a href="/wiki/Centaur_(rocket_stage)" title="Centaur (rocket stage)">\n        Centaur-G\n       </a>\n       booster (cancelled after the loss of\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The retention of the internal airlock allowed NASA to use\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-109" title="STS-109">\n        STS-109\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       servicing mission, along with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Astrotech_Corporation" title="Astrotech Corporation">\n        Spacehab\n       </a>\n       double module used on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       . Due to\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'s\n       </i>\n       heavier weight, it was less ideal for NASA to use it for missions to the International Space Station, though modifications were made to the Shuttle during its last refit in case the spacecraft was needed for such tasks.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thermal_protection_system">\n        Thermal protection system\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Thermal protection system">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Externally,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was the first orbiter in the fleet whose surface was mostly covered with High &amp; Low Temperature Reusable Surface Insulation (HRSI/LRSI) tiles as its main\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space Shuttle thermal protection system">\n        thermal protection system\n       </a>\n       (TPS), with white silicone rubber-painted\n       <a href="/wiki/Nomex" title="Nomex">\n        Nomex\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 known as Felt Reusable Surface Insulation (FRSI) blankets \xe2\x80\x93 in some areas on the wings, fuselage and payload bay doors. FRSI once covered almost 25% of the orbiter; the first upgrade resulted in its removal from many areas, and in later flights it was only used on the upper section of the payload bay doors and inboard sections of the upper wing surfaces.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OTPS_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OTPS-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The upgrade also involved replacing many of the white LRSI tiles on the upper surfaces with Advanced Flexible Reusable Surface Insulation (AFRSI) blankets (also known as Fibrous Insulation Blankets, or FIBs) that had been used on\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       . Originally,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       had 32,000 tiles \xe2\x80\x93 the upgrade reduced this to 24,300. The AFRSI blankets consisted of layers of pure silica felt sandwiched between a layer of silica fabric on the outside and S-Glass fabric on the inside, stitched together using pure silica thread in a 1-inch grid, then coated with a high-purity silica coating. The blankets were semi-rigid and could be made as large as 30" by 30". Each blanket replaced as many as 25 tiles and was bonded directly to the orbiter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OTPS_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OTPS-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The direct application of the blankets to the orbiter resulted in weight reduction, improved durability, reduced fabrication and installation cost, and reduced installation schedule time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All of this work was performed during\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'s\n       </i>\n       first retrofitting and the post-\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       stand-down.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="852" data-file-width="1009" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg/330px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg/440px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-28_in_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         landing at\n         <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n          Edwards Air Force Base\n         </a>\n         following\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-28" title="STS-28">\n          STS-28\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Despite refinements to the orbiter\'s thermal protection system and other enhancements,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       would never weigh as little unloaded as the other orbiters in the fleet. The next-oldest shuttle,\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , was also relatively heavy, although 2,200\xc2\xa0lb (1,000\xc2\xa0kg) lighter than\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Markings_and_insignia">\n        Markings and insignia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Markings and insignia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Until its last refit,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was the only operational orbiter with wing markings consisting of an American flag on the port (left) wing and the letters "USA" on the starboard (right) wing.\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       all, until 1998, bore markings consisting of the letters "USA" below an American flag on the left wing, and the pre-1998\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_logo" title="NASA logo">\n        NASA "worm" logo\n       </a>\n       afore the respective orbiter\'s name on the right wing. (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">\n         Enterprise\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , the test vehicle which was the prototype for\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       , originally had the same wing markings as\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       but with the letters "USA" on the right wing spaced closer together;\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\'\n       </i>\n       s markings were modified to match\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       in 1983.) The name of the orbiter was originally placed on the payload bay doors much like\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       but was placed on the crew cabin after the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       disaster so that the orbiter could be easily identified while in orbit. From its last refit to its destruction,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       bore markings identical to those of its operational sister orbiters \xe2\x80\x93 the NASA "meatball" logo on the left wing and the American flag afore the orbiter\'s name on the right; only\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'s\n       </i>\n       distinctive wing "chines" remained. These black areas on the upper surfaces of the shuttle\'s forward wing were added because, at first, shuttle designers did not know how reentry heating would affect the craft\'s upper wing surfaces.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The "chines" allowed\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       to be easily recognized at a distance, as opposed to the subsequent orbiters. The "chines" were added after\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       arrived at KSC in 1979.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="SILTS_pod">\n        SILTS pod\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: SILTS pod">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Another unique external feature, termed the "SILTS" pod, was located on the top of\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'s\n       </i>\n       vertical stabilizer, and was installed after\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-9" title="STS-9">\n        STS-9\n       </a>\n       to acquire infrared and other thermal data. Though the pod\'s equipment was removed after initial tests, NASA decided to leave it in place, mainly to save costs, along with the agency\'s plans to use it for future experiments. The vertical stabilizer was later modified to incorporate the drag chute first used on\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       in 1992.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_upgrades">\n        Other upgrades\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other upgrades">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="778" data-file-width="1105" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg/330px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg/440px-Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_lands_following_STS-62_on_18_March_1994..jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         landing at the\n         <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n          Kennedy Space Center\n         </a>\n         following\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-62" title="STS-62">\n          STS-62\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was also originally fitted with\n       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Corporation" title="Lockheed Corporation">\n        Lockheed\n       </a>\n       -built ejection seats identical to those found on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SR-71_Blackbird" title="SR-71 Blackbird">\n        SR-71 Blackbird\n       </a>\n       . These were active for the four orbital test flights, but deactivated after\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-4" title="STS-4">\n        STS-4\n       </a>\n       , and removed entirely after\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-9" title="STS-9">\n        STS-9\n       </a>\n       .\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was also the only spaceworthy orbiter not delivered with\n       <a href="/wiki/Head-up_display" title="Head-up display">\n        head-up displays\n       </a>\n       for the Commander and Pilot, although these were incorporated after STS-9. Like its sister ships,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was eventually retrofitted with the new MEDS "\n       <a href="/wiki/Glass_cockpit" title="Glass cockpit">\n        glass cockpit\n       </a>\n       " display and lightweight seats.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future">\n        Future\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Future">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-109_launch.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2998" data-file-width="3000" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/STS-109_launch.jpg/220px-STS-109_launch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/STS-109_launch.jpg/330px-STS-109_launch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/STS-109_launch.jpg/440px-STS-109_launch.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-109_launch.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         launches on STS-109(HST-3B), its final successful mission\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Had\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       not been destroyed, it would have been fitted with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Androgynous_Peripheral_Attach_System#APAS-95" title="Androgynous Peripheral Attach System">\n        external airlock/docking adapter\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       , an\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       assembly mission, originally planned for November 2003.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was scheduled for this mission due to\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       being out of service for its Orbital Maintenance Down Period, and because the ISS assembly schedule could not be adhered to with only\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x99s \'career\' would have started to wind down after\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       . It was to service the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       two more times between 2004 and 2005, but no more missions were planned for it again except for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cancelled_Space_Shuttle_missions" title="Cancelled Space Shuttle missions">\n        a mission designated STS-144\n       </a>\n       where it would retrieve the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       from orbit and bring it back to\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Following the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       accident, NASA flew the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       mission using\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n         Atlantis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , combining the planned fourth and fifth servicing missions into one final mission to Hubble. Because of the retirement of the Space Shuttle fleet, the batteries and gyroscopes that keep the telescope pointed will eventually fail also because of the magnifier screen, which would result in its reentry and break-up in Earth\'s atmosphere. A "Soft Capture Docking Mechanism", based on the docking adapter that was to be used on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion spacecraft\n       </a>\n       , was installed during the last servicing mission in anticipation of this event.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was also scheduled to launch the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_X-38" title="NASA X-38">\n        X-38\n       </a>\n       V-201 Crew Return Vehicle prototype as the next mission after STS-118, until the cancellation of the project in 2002.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flights">\n        Flights\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flights">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       flew 28 missions, gathering 300.74 days spent in space with 4,808 orbits and a total distance of 125,204,911 miles (201,497,772\xc2\xa0km) up until STS-107.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite being in service during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle%E2%80%93Mir_Program" title="Shuttle\xe2\x80\x93Mir Program">\n        Shuttle-Mir\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       programs,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       did not fly any missions that visited a space station. The other three active orbiters at the time had visited both\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n         Mir\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       at least once.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was not suited for high-inclination missions.\n      </p>\n      <table border="1" class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="background:#efefef;">\n         #\n        </th>\n        <th  STS-9\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         39-A\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n          Edwards Air See\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n            STS-107\n           </a>\n           )\n          </center>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </center>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Final_mission_and_destruction">\n        Final mission and destruction\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Final mission and destruction">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Columbia disaster\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_STS-107,_official_photo.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3277" data-file-width="4096" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg/220px-Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg/330px-Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg/440px-Crew_of_STS-107%2C_official_photo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_STS-107,_official_photo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The crew of STS-107 in October 2001. From left to right:\n         <a href="/wiki/David_M._Brown" title="David M. Brown">\n          Brown\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Rick_Husband" title="Rick Husband">\n          Husband\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Laurel_Clark" title="Laurel Clark">\n          Clark\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Kalpana_Chawla" title="Kalpana Chawla">\n          Chawla\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Michael_P._Anderson" title="Michael P. Anderson">\n          Anderson\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/William_C._McCool" title="William C. McCool">\n          McCool\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Ramon" title="Ilan Ramon">\n          Ramon\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbia_Memorial.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2334" data-file-width="1907" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Columbia_Memorial.JPG/170px-Columbia_Memorial.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Columbia_Memorial.JPG/255px-Columbia_Memorial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Columbia_Memorial.JPG/340px-Columbia_Memorial.JPG 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbia_Memorial.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n         memorial in\n         <a href="/wiki/Arlington_National_Cemetery" title="Arlington National Cemetery">\n          Arlington National Cemetery\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was destroyed at about 09:00\n       <a href="/wiki/Time_zone#UTC-5_.28EST_-_Eastern_Standard_Time.29" title="Time zone">\n        EST\n       </a>\n       on February 1, 2003 while re-entering the atmosphere after a\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        16-day scientific mission\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Accident_Investigation_Board" title="Columbia Accident Investigation Board">\n        Columbia Accident Investigation Board\n       </a>\n       determined that a hole was punctured in the leading edge on one of\n       <i>\n        Columbia\'s\n       </i>\n       wings, made of a carbon\n       <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_carbon%E2%80%93carbon" title="Reinforced carbon\xe2\x80\x93carbon">\n        composite\n       </a>\n       . The hole had formed when a piece of insulating foam from the external fuel tank peeled off during the launch 16 days earlier and struck the shuttle\'s left wing. During the intense heat of re-entry, hot gases penetrated the interior of the wing, likely compromising the hydraulic system and leading to control failure of the control surfaces. The resulting loss of control exposed minimally protected areas of the orbiter to full-entry heating and dynamic pressures that eventually led to vehicle break up.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The nearly 84,000 pieces of collected debris of the vessel are stored in a 16th floor office suite in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       . The collection was opened to the media once and has since been open only to researchers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Unlike\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       , which had a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        replacement orbiter\n       </a>\n       built,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       did not.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The seven crew members who died aboard this final mission were:\n       <a href="/wiki/Rick_Husband" title="Rick Husband">\n        Rick Husband\n       </a>\n       , Commander;\n       <a href="/wiki/William_C._McCool" title="William C. McCool">\n        William C. McCool\n       </a>\n       , Pilot;\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_P._Anderson" title="Michael P. Anderson">\n        Michael P. Anderson\n       </a>\n       , Payload Commander/Mission Specialist 3;\n       <a href="/wiki/David_M._Brown" title="David M. Brown">\n        David M. Brown\n       </a>\n       , Mission Specialist 1;\n       <a href="/wiki/Kalpana_Chawla" title="Kalpana Chawla">\n        Kalpana Chawla\n       </a>\n       , Mission Specialist 2;\n       <a href="/wiki/Laurel_Clark" title="Laurel Clark">\n        Laurel Clark\n       </a>\n       , Mission Specialist 4; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Ramon" title="Ilan Ramon">\n        Ilan Ramon\n       </a>\n       , Payload Specialist 1.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes_and_memorials">\n        Tributes and memorials\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tributes and memorials">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Patricia Huffman Smith Museum\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The debris field encompassed hundreds of miles across\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Texas" title="Northeast Texas">\n        Northeast Texas\n       </a>\n       and into\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       . The nose cap and remains of all seven crew members were found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Sabine_County,_Texas" title="Sabine County, Texas">\n        Sabine County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Texas" title="East Texas">\n        East Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To honor those who lost their lives aboard the shuttle and during the recovery efforts, the\n       <a class="external text" href="http://nasacolumbiamuseum.com/" rel="nofollow">\n        Patricia Huffman Smith NASA Museum\n       </a>\n       "Remembering Columbia" was opened in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hemphill,_Texas" title="Hemphill, Texas">\n        Hemphill\n       </a>\n       , Sabine County, Texas. The museum tells the story of Space Shuttle Columbia explorations throughout all its missions, including the final STS-107. Its exhibits also show the efforts of local citizens during the recovery period of the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       shuttle debris and its crew\'s remains. An area is dedicated to each STS-107 crew member, and also to the Texas Forest Service helicopter pilot who died in the recovery effort. The museum houses many objects and artifacts from: NASA and its contractors; the families of the STS-107 crew; and other individuals. The crew\'s families contributed personal items of the crew members to be on permanent display. The museum features two interactive simulator displays that emulate activities of the shuttle and orbiter. The digital learning center and its classroom provide educational opportunities for all ages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Columbia Memorial Space Center\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Memorial_Space_Center" title="Columbia Memorial Space Center">\n        Columbia Memorial Space Center\n       </a>\n       is the U.S. national memorial for the Space Shuttle Columbia\xe2\x80\x99s seven crew members. It is located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Downey,_California" title="Downey, California">\n        Downey\n       </a>\n       on the site of the Space Shuttle\'s origins and production, the former\n       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aviation#Space_program_and_acquisitions" title="North American Aviation">\n        North American Aviation\n       </a>\n       plant in Los Angeles County, southern California. The facility is also a hands-on learning center with interactive exhibits, workshops, and classes about\n       <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_space_science" title="Outline of space science">\n        space science\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronautics" title="Astronautics">\n        astronautics\n       </a>\n       , and the Space Shuttle program\'s legacy \xe2\x80\x94 providing educational opportunities for all ages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Naming dedications\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle\'s final crew was honored in 2003 when the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Board_on_Geographic_Names" title="United States Board on Geographic Names">\n        United States Board on Geographic Names\n       </a>\n       approved the name\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Point" title="Columbia Point">\n        Columbia Point\n       </a>\n       for a 13,980-foot (4,260\xc2\xa0m) mountain in Colorado\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Sangre_de_Cristo_Mountains" title="Sangre de Cristo Mountains">\n        Sangre de Cristo Mountains\n       </a>\n       , less than a half-mile from\n       <a href="/wiki/Challenger_Point" title="Challenger Point">\n        Challenger Point\n       </a>\n       , a peak named after America\'s other lost shuttle. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Hills_(Mars)" title="Columbia Hills (Mars)">\n        Columbia Hills\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       were also named in honor of the crew, and a host of\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster#Memorials" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        other memorials\n       </a>\n       were dedicated in various forms.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_(supercomputer)" title="Columbia (supercomputer)">\n        Columbia supercomputer\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Advanced_Supercomputing_Division" title="NASA Advanced Supercomputing Division">\n        NASA Advanced Supercomputing (NAS) Division\n       </a>\n       located at\n       <a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">\n        Ames Research Center\n       </a>\n       in California was named in honor of the crew lost in the 2003 disaster. Built as a joint effort between NASA and technical partners\n       <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">\n        SGI\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">\n        Intel\n       </a>\n       in 2004, the supercomputer was used in scientific research of space, the Earth\'s climate, and aerodynamic design of space launch vehicles and aircraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first part of the system, built in 2003, was dedicated to STS-107 astronaut and engineer Kalpana Chawla, who prior to joining the Space Shuttle program worked at Ames Research Center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_tributes">\n        Media tributes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Media tributes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Guitarist\n       <a href="/wiki/Steve_Morse" title="Steve Morse">\n        Steve Morse\n       </a>\n       of the rock band\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">\n        Deep Purple\n       </a>\n       wrote the instrumental "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contact_Lost" title="Contact Lost">\n        Contact Lost\n       </a>\n       " in response to the news of the tragedy, recorded by Deep Purple and featured as the closing track on their 2003 album "\n       <a href="/wiki/Bananas_(album)" title="Bananas (album)">\n        Bananas\n       </a>\n       ". It was dedicated to the astronauts whose lives were lost in the disaster. Morse donated songwriting royalties to the families of lost astronauts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuitarSite_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GuitarSite-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Astronaut and mission specialist engineer\n       <a href="/wiki/Kalpana_Chawla" title="Kalpana Chawla">\n        Kalpana Chawla\n       </a>\n       , one of the victims of the accident, was a fan of Deep Purple and had exchanged e-mails with the band during the flight, making the tragedy even more personal for the group.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuitarSite_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GuitarSite-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       She took three CDs into space with her, two of which were Deep Purple albums (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Machine_Head_(album)" title="Machine Head (album)">\n         Machine Head\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Purpendicular" title="Purpendicular">\n         Purpendicular\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ). Both CDs survived the destruction of the shuttle and the 39-mile plunge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The musical group Echo\'s Children included singer-songwriter Cat Faber\'s "Columbia" on their final album\n       <i>\n        From the Hazel Tree\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Long_Winters" title="The Long Winters">\n        The Long Winters\n       </a>\n       band\'s 2005 album\n       <i>\n        Ultimatum\n       </i>\n       features the song "The Commander Thinks Aloud", a tribute to the final\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Eric_Johnson" title="Eric Johnson">\n        Eric Johnson\n       </a>\n       instrumental "Columbia" from his 2005 album\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bloom_(Eric_Johnson_album)" title="Bloom (Eric Johnson album)">\n         Bloom\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was written as a commemoration and tribute to the lives that were lost. Johnson said "I wanted to make it more of a positive message, a salute, a celebration rather than just concentrating on a few moments of tragedy, but instead the bigger picture of these brave people\xe2\x80\x99s lives."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The graphic novel\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_(comics)" title="Orbiter (comics)">\n        <i>\n         Orbiter\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Warren_Ellis" title="Warren Ellis">\n        Warren Ellis\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Colleen_Doran" title="Colleen Doran">\n        Colleen Doran\n       </a>\n       was dedicated to the "lives, memories and legacies of the seven astronauts lost on space shuttle\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       during mission STS-107."\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Laurel_Clark" title="Laurel Clark">\n        Laurel Clark\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x99s wake up call on STS \xe2\x80\x93 107 was\n       <a href="/wiki/Runrig" title="Runrig">\n        Runrig\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x99s "Running to the Light". Laurel took\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Stamping_Ground" title="The Stamping Ground">\n        The Stamping Ground\n       </a>\n       CD into space with her and when the Shuttle exploded the CD was found back on Earth, and presented to the band. The bands last Studio Album,\n       <i>\n        The Story\n       </i>\n       , final track, "Somewhere", ends with a recording of her voice introducing the song.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">\n        Popular culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Popular culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Fans of the original\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">\n          Star Trek\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        television series were largely responsible for\n        <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n         NASA\n        </a>\n        naming the first\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n        <i>\n         Enterprise\n        </i>\n        . In the television series\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Enterprise" title="Star Trek: Enterprise">\n          Star Trek: Enterprise\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        both the first and second starships of the human-built\n        <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_(NX-01)" title="Enterprise (NX-01)">\n         NX-Class\n        </a>\n        , registry numbers NX-01 &amp; NX-02 respectively, were named in honor of pre-existing\n        <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n         NASA\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttles\n        </a>\n        . The second vessel\'s name was first revealed in the season 3 episode "\n        <a href="/wiki/E%C2%B2" title="E\xc2\xb2">\n         E\xc2\xb2\n        </a>\n        " to be\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Home_(Star_Trek:_Enterprise)" title="Home (Star Trek: Enterprise)">\n          Columbia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , in honor of the Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        following its destruction on February 1, 2003. The uniforms on NX-02\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        bear a crew patch depicting 7 stars, in honor of the astronauts who died in the accident.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In\n        <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Red_and_Blue" title="Pok\xc3\xa9mon Red and Blue">\n         <i>\n          Pok\xc3\xa9mon Red\n         </i>\n         and\n         <i>\n          Blue\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        and\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Yellow" title="Pok\xc3\xa9mon Yellow">\n          Pok\xc3\xa9mon Yellow\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        a model of the Space Shuttle can be seen on the second floor of the Pewter City Museum. While\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        was identified by name in the original games, in the 2004\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enhanced_remakes" title="Enhanced remakes">\n         remakes\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_FireRed_and_LeafGreen" title="Pok\xc3\xa9mon FireRed and LeafGreen">\n         <i>\n          Pok\xc3\xa9mon FireRed\n         </i>\n         and\n         <i>\n          LeafGreen\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        , the model was simply identified as "Space Shuttle". The 2016 release for 3DS did not censor the name.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A restored\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        was used in episode 19 ("Wild Horses") of the anime\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cowboy_Bebop" title="Cowboy Bebop">\n          Cowboy Bebop\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        to rescue Spike when his Swordfish enters a steep orbit and is going to burn up. After the rescue, the shuttle crash-lands after losing heat-resistant tiles. The anime, made in 1998, predated the\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster by five years.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ghostlightning_27-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ghostlightning-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The beginning of\n        <a href="/wiki/Kate_Bush" title="Kate Bush">\n         Kate Bush\n        </a>\n        \'s song\n        <i>\n         Hello Earth\n        </i>\n        , from the\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hounds_of_Love" title="Hounds of Love">\n          Hounds of Love\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        album, samples signals to and from\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        during a re-entry during the early 1980s.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Homer_Hickam" title="Homer Hickam">\n         Homer Hickam\n        </a>\n        \'s novel\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Moon" title="Back to the Moon">\n          Back to the Moon\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        is mostly set on\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        . The structural differences between\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        and the other shuttles is central to the plot.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In the finale of the first season of\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">\n          The West Wing\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , "\n        <a href="/wiki/What_Kind_of_Day_Has_It_Been" title="What Kind of Day Has It Been">\n         What Kind of Day Has It Been\n        </a>\n        ",\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        does not land on schedule due to technical problems with a door mechanism.\n        <a href="/wiki/Toby_Ziegler" title="Toby Ziegler">\n         Toby Ziegler\n        </a>\n        \'s brother is on board. The shuttle lands successfully by the end of the episode.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The rock band\n        <a href="/wiki/Rush_(band)" title="Rush (band)">\n         Rush\n        </a>\n        wrote and recorded the song "\n        <a href="/wiki/Countdown_(Rush_song)" title="Countdown (Rush song)">\n         Countdown\n        </a>\n        " about the launch of STS-1. All three members of the group were present at the launch, and the credits of the album\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Signals_(Rush_album)" title="Signals (Rush album)">\n          Signals\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        dedicated the song to "the astronauts Young &amp; Crippen and all the people of NASA for their inspiration and cooperation."\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The shuttle features in opening chapters of the 1997\n        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Baxter_(author)" title="Stephen Baxter (author)">\n         Stephen Baxter\n        </a>\n        novel \'\n        <a href="/wiki/Titan_(Baxter_novel)" title="Titan (Baxter novel)">\n         Titan\n        </a>\n        \', where it is portrayed carrying out mission STS-143.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Crew members from Mission\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-73" title="STS-73">\n         STS-73\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Ken_Bowersox" title="Ken Bowersox">\n         Ken Bowersox\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_G._Coleman" title="Catherine G. Coleman">\n         Catherine G. Coleman\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_C._Thornton" title="Kathryn C. Thornton">\n         Kathryn C. Thornton\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Frederick_W._Leslie" title="Frederick W. Leslie">\n         Frederick W. Leslie\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Albert_Sacco" title="Albert Sacco">\n         Albert Sacco\n        </a>\n        ) were featured in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Home_Improvement_(TV_series)" title="Home Improvement (TV series)">\n         <i>\n          Home Improvement\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        television show in the episode\n        <a href="/wiki/List_of_Home_Improvement_episodes" title="List of Home Improvement episodes">\n         "Fear of Flying"\n        </a>\n        as well as scenes from the shuttle mission.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n
